Exceptions will cause the\\n224:      * pipeline to be recognized as failed, because the last data items are not processed properly.\\n225:      * You may use this method to flush remaining buffered elements in the state into the current\\n226:      * transaction which will be committed in the last checkpoint.\\n227:      */\\n228:     protected void finishProcessing(@Nullable TXN transaction) {}\\n229: \\n230:     // ------ entry points for above methods implementing {@CheckPointedFunction} and\\n231:     // {@CheckpointListener} ------\\n232: \\n233:     /** This should not be implemented by subclasses. */\\n234:     @Override\\n235:     public final void invoke(IN value) throws Exception {}\\n236: \\n237:     @Override\\n238:     public final void invoke(IN value, Context context) throws Exception {\\n239:         TXN currentTransaction = currentTransaction();\\n240:         checkNotNull(\\n241:                 currentTransaction,\\n242:                 \\\"Two phase commit sink function with null transaction should not be invoked! \\\");\\n243:         invoke(currentTransaction, value, context);\\n244:     }\\n245: \\n246:     @Override\\n247:     public final void finish() throws Exception {\\n248:         finished = true;\\n249:         finishProcessing(currentTransaction());\\n250:     }\\n251: \\n252:     @Override\\n253:     public final void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\\n254:         // the following scenarios are possible here\\n255:         //\\n256:         //  (1) there is exactly one transaction from the latest checkpoint that\\n257:         //      was triggered and completed. That should be the common case.\\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\\n259:         //\\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\\n262:         //      for example when:\\n263:         //\\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n267:         //\\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\\n272:         //\\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\\n277:         //\\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\\n283:         //\\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\\n285:         //\\n286: \\n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\\n290: \\n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\\n296:                 continue;\\n297:             }\\n298: \\n299:             LOG.info(\\n300:                     \\\"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\\\",\\n301:                     name(),\\n302:                     checkpointId,\\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\\n305: \\n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\\n307:             try {\\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\\n311:                     firstError = t;\\n312:                 }\\n313:             }\\n314: \\n315:             LOG.debug(\\\"{} - committed checkpoint transaction {}\\\", name(), pendingTransaction);\\n316: \\n317:             pendingTransactionIterator.remove();\\n318:         }\\n319: \\n320:         if (firstError != null) {\\n321:             throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\\n322:                     \\\"Committing one of transactions failed, logging first encountered failure\\\",\\n323:                     firstError);\\n324:         }\\n325:     }\\n326: \\n327:     @Override\\n328:     public void notifyCheckpointAborted(long checkpointId) {}\\n329: \\n330:     @Override\\n331:     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\\n332:         // this is like the pre-commit of a 2-phase-commit transaction\\n333:         // we are ready to commit and remember the transaction\\n334: \\n335:         long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\\n336:         LOG.debug(\\n337:                 \\\"{} - checkpoint {} triggered, flushing transaction '{}'\\\",\\n338:                 name(),\\n339:                 context.getCheckpointId(),\\n340:                 currentTransactionHolder);\\n341: \\n342:         if (currentTransactionHolder != null) {\\n343:             preCommit(currentTransactionHolder.handle);\\n344: }\\n347: \\n348:         // no need to start new transactions after sink function is closed (no more input data)\\n349:         if (!finished) {\\n350:             currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\\n351:         } else {\\n352:             currentTransactionHolder = null;\\n353:         }\\n354:         LOG.debug(\\\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\\\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\\n355: \\n356:         state.update(\\n357:                 Collections.singletonList(\\n358:                         new State<>(\\n359:                                 this.currentTransactionHolder,\\n360:                                 new ArrayList<>(pendingCommitTransactions.values()),\\n361:                                 userContext)));\\n362:     }\\n363: \\n364:     @Override\\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\\n367:         // the\\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\\n370: \\n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\\n373: \\n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a scale-out event, where some of the\\n376:         // new task do not have and transactions assigned to check)\\n377: \\n378:         // we can have more than one transaction to check in case of a scale-in event, or\\n379:         // for the reasons discussed in the 'notifyCheckpointComplete()' method.\\n380: \\n381:         state = Pre commit must make all of the necessary steps to\n179:      * prepare the transaction for a commit that might happen in the future. After this point the\n180:      * transaction might still be aborted, but underlying implementation must ensure that commit\n181:      * calls on already pre committed transactions will always succeed.\n182:      *\n183:      * <p>Usually implementation involves flushing the data.\n184:      */\n185:     protected abstract void preCommit(TXN transaction) throws Exception;\n186: \n187:     /**\n188:      * Commit a pre-committed transaction. User implementation must ensure that this\n196:      * call will eventually succeed. If it fails, Flink application will be restarted and it will be\n197:      * invoked again. If it does not succeed eventually, a data loss will occur. Transactions will\n198:      * be recovered in an order in which they were created.\n199:      */\n200:     protected void recoverAndCommit(TXN transaction) {\n201:         commit(transaction);\n202:     }\n203: \n204:     /** Abort a transaction. */\n205:     protected abstract void abort(TXN transaction);\n206: \n207:     /** Abort a transaction that was rejected by a coordinator after a failure. */\n208:     protected void recoverAndAbort(TXN transaction) {\n209:         abort(transaction);\n210:     }\n211: \n212:     /**\n213:      * Callback for subclasses which is called after restoring (each) user context.\n214:      *\n215:      * @param handledTransactions transactions which were already committed or aborted and do not\n216:      *     need further handling\n217:      */\n218:     protected void finishRecoveringContext(Collection<TXN> handledTransactions) {}\n219: \n220:     /**\n221:      * This method is called at the end of data processing.\n222:      *\n223:      * <p>The method is expected to flush all remaining buffered data. Exceptions will cause the\n224:      * pipeline to be recognized as failed, because the last data items are not processed properly.\n225:      * You may use this method to flush remaining buffered elements in the state into the current\n226:      * transaction which will be committed in the last checkpoint.\n227:      */\n228:     protected void finishProcessing(@Nullable TXN transaction) {}\n229: \n230:     // ------ entry points for above methods implementing {@CheckPointedFunction} and\n231:     // {@CheckpointListener} ------\n232: \n233:     /** This should not be implemented by subclasses. */\n234:     @Override\n235:     public final void invoke(IN value) throws Exception {}\n236: \n237:     @Override\n238:     public final void invoke(IN value, Context context) throws Exception {\n239:         TXN currentTransaction = currentTransaction();\n240:         checkNotNull(\n241:                 currentTransaction,\n242:                 \"Two phase commit sink function with null transaction should not be invoked! \");\n243:         invoke(currentTransaction, value, context);\n244:     }\n245: \n246:     @Override\n247:     public final void finish() throws Exception {\n248:         finished = true;\n249:         finishProcessing(currentTransaction());\n250:     }\n251: \n252:     @Override\n253:     public final void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {\n254:         // the following scenarios are possible here\n255:         //\n256:         //  (1) there is exactly one transaction from the latest checkpoint that\n257:         //      was triggered and completed. That should be the common case.\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\n259:         //\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\n262:         //      for example when:\n263:         //\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n267:         //\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n272:         //\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\n277:         //\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\n283:         //\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\n285:         //\n286: \n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\n290: \n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\n296:                 continue;\n297:             }\n298: \n299:             LOG.info(\n300:                     \"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\",\n301:                     name(),\n302:                     checkpointId,\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\n305: \n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\n307:             try {\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\n311:                     firstError = t;\n312:                 }\n313:             }\n314: \n315:             LOG.debug(\"{} - committed checkpoint transaction {}\", name(), pendingTransaction);\n316: \n317:             pendingTransactionIterator.remove();\n318:         }\n319: \n320:         if (firstError != null) {\n321:             throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\n322:                     \"Committing one of transactions failed, logging first encountered failure\",\n323:                     firstError);\n324:         }\n325:     }\n326: \n327:     @Override\n328:     public void notifyCheckpointAborted(long checkpointId) {}\n329: \n330:     @Override\n331:     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n332:         // this is like the pre-commit of a 2-phase-commit transaction\n333:         // we are ready to commit and remember the transaction\n334: \n335:         long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\n336:         LOG.debug(\n337:                 \"{} - checkpoint {} triggered, flushing transaction '{}'\",\n338:                 name(),\n339:                 context.getCheckpointId(),\n340:                 currentTransactionHolder);\n341: \n342:         if (currentTransactionHolder != null) {\n343:             preCommit(currentTransactionHolder.handle);\n344:             pendingCommitTransactions.put(checkpointId, currentTransactionHolder);\n345:             LOG.debug(\"{} - stored pending transactions {}\", name(), pendingCommitTransactions);\n346:         }\n347: \n348:         // no need to start new transactions after sink function is closed (no more input data)\n349:         if (!finished) {\n350:             currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\n351:         } else {\n352:             currentTransactionHolder = null;\n353:         }\n354:         LOG.debug(\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\n355: \n356:         state.update(\n357:                 Collections.singletonList(\n358:                         new State<>(\n359:                                 this.currentTransactionHolder,\n360:                                 new ArrayList<>(pendingCommitTransactions.values()),\n361:                                 userContext)));\n362:     }\n363: \n364:     @Override\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\n367:         // the\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\n370: \n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\n373: \n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a scale-out event, where some of the\n376:         // new task do not have and transactions assigned to check)\n377: \n378:         // we can have more than one transaction to check in case of a scale-in event, or\n379:         // for the reasons discussed in the 'notifyCheckpointComplete()' method.\n380: \n381:         state = context.getOperatorStateStore().getListState(stateDescriptor);\n382: \n383:         boolean recoveredUserContext = false;\n384:         if (context.isRestored()) {\n385:             LOG.info(\"{} - restoring state\", name());\n386:             for (State<TXN, CONTEXT> operatorState : state.get()) {\n387:                 userContext = operatorState.getContext();\n388:                 List<TransactionHolder<TXN>> recoveredTransactions =\n389:                         operatorState.getPendingCommitTransactions();\n390:                 List<TXN> handledTransactions = new ArrayList<>(recoveredTransactions.size() + 1);\n391:                 for (TransactionHolder<TXN> recoveredTransaction : recoveredTransactions) {\n392:                     // If this fails to succeed eventually, there is actually data loss\n393:                     recoverAndCommitInternal(recoveredTransaction);\n394:                     handledTransactions.add(recoveredTransaction.handle);\n395:                     LOG.info(\"{} committed recovered transaction {}\", name(), recoveredTransaction);\n396:                 }\n397: \n398:                 {\n399:                     if (operatorState.getPendingTransaction() != null) {\n400:                         TXN transaction = operatorState.getPendingTransaction().handle;\n401:                         recoverAndAbort(transaction);\n402:                         handledTransactions.add(transaction);\n403:                         LOG.info(\n404:                                 \"{} aborted recovered transaction {}\",\n405:                                 name(),\n406:                                 operatorState.getPendingTransaction());\n407:                     }\n408:                 }\n409: \n410:                 if (userContext.isPresent()) {\n411:                     finishRecoveringContext(handledTransactions);\n412:                     recoveredUserContext = true;\n413:                 }\n414:             }\n415:         }\n416: \n417:         // if in restore we didn't get any userContext or we are initializing from scratch\n418:         if (!recoveredUserContext) {\n419:             LOG.info(\"{} - no state to restore\", name());\n420: \n421:             userContext = initializeUserContext();\n422:         }\n423:         this.pendingCommitTransactions.clear();\n424: \n425:         currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\n426:         LOG.debug(\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\n427:     }\n428: \n429:     /**\n430:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #beginTransaction()} to ensure that the\n431:      * {@link TransactionHolder} is created at the same time.\n432:      */\n433:     private TransactionHolder<TXN> beginTransactionInternal() throws Exception {\n434:         return new TransactionHolder<>(beginTransaction(), clock.millis());\n435:     }\n436: \n437:     /**\n438:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #recoverAndCommit(Object)} to ensure that\n439:      * the configuration parameters {@link #transactionTimeout} and {@link\n440:      * #ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout} are respected.\n441:      */\n442:     private void recoverAndCommitInternal(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\n443:         try {\n444:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(transactionHolder);\n445:             recoverAndCommit(transactionHolder.handle);\n446:         } catch (final Exception e) {\n447:             final long elapsedTime = clock.millis() - transactionHolder.transactionStartTime;\n448:             if (ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout && elapsedTime > transactionTimeout) {\n449:                 LOG.error(\n450:                         \"Error while committing transaction {}. \"\n451:                                 + \"Transaction has been open for longer than the transaction timeout ({}).\"\n452:                                 + \"Commit will not be attempted again. Data loss might have occurred.\",\n453:                         transactionHolder.handle,\n454:                         transactionTimeout,\n455:                         e);\n456:             } else {\n457:                 throw e;\n458:             }\n459:         }\n460:     }\n461: \n462:     private void logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\n463:         final long elapsedTime = transactionHolder.elapsedTime(clock);\n464:         if (transactionTimeoutWarningRatio >= 0\n465:                 && elapsedTime > transactionTimeout * transactionTimeoutWarningRatio) {\n466:             LOG.warn(\n467:                     \"Transaction {} has been open for {} ms. \"\n468:                             + \"This is close to or even exceeding the transaction timeout of {} ms.\",\n469:                     transactionHolder.handle,\n470:                     elapsedTime,\n471:                     transactionTimeout);\n472:         }\n473:     }\n474: \n475:     @Override\n476:     public void close() throws Exception {\n477:         super.close();\n478: \n479:         TXN currentTransaction = currentTransaction();\n480:         if (currentTransaction != null) {\n481:             abort(currentTransaction);\n482:         }\n483: \n484:         currentTransactionHolder = null;\n485:     }\n486: \n487:     /**\n488:      * Sets the transaction timeout. files within buckets. This is integrated\\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\\n74:  * prefix \\\"prefix\\\" and a suffix \\\".ext\\\", a file named {@code \\\"prefix-1-17.ext\\\"} contains the data\\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\\n76:  *\\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\\n80:  *\\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\\n90:  *\\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\\n99:  */\\n100: @Internal\\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\\n103: \\n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\\n105: \\n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\\n107: \\n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\\n109: \\n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ? extends BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ?>> bucketsBuilder;\\n111: \\n112:     // --------------------------- runtime fields -----------------------------\\n113: \\n114:     private transient StreamingFileSinkHelper<IN> helper;\\n115: \\n116:     /**\\n117:      * Creates a new {@code StreamingFileSink} that writes files to the given base directory with\\n118:      * the give buckets properties.\\n119:      */\\n120:     @VisibleForTesting\\n121:     public StreamingFileSink(\\n122:             BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ? In order to instantiate the sink, call {@link RowFormatBuilder#build()} after\\n144:      *     specifying the desired parameters.\\n145:      */\\n146:     @Internal\\n147:     public static <IN> StreamingFileSink.DefaultRowFormatBuilder<IN> forRowFormat(\\n148:             final Path basePath, final Encoder<IN> encoder) {\\n149:         return new DefaultRowFormatBuilder<>(basePath, encoder, new DateTimeBucketAssigner<>());\\n150:     }\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/functions/sink/filesystem/legacy/StreamingFileSink.java%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"478a1eb2-3c2e-4179-876a-c821c97a7690","uuid":"aee3d744-113c-401f-821e-20fa8625101e","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one\\n3:  * or more contributor license agreements.
